# Stack Protection Mechanisms in LLVM

## Your Task

Find all C++ source files in `llvm/llvm-project` that implement stack protection mechanisms against buffer overflow attacks. Specifically identify: 1. The LLVM pass that inserts stack protector checks (look for `StackProtector` in `llvm/lib/CodeGen/`). 2. The file that defines the `SafeStack` pass that separates safe and unsafe stack allocations (under `llvm/lib/CodeGen/`). 3. The header file that declares the stack protection pass interface. 4. The compiler-rt runtime file that provides the `__stack_chk_fail` implementation (look under `compiler-rt/lib/builtins/`). 5. Any file in `llvm/lib/Transforms/Instrumentation/` that implements memory safety instrumentation related to stack frame protection. Report the repo, file path, and the primary function or class handling stack protection for each.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the security domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `github.com/llvm/llvm-project` (llvm/llvm-project)
- `github.com/gcc-mirror/gcc` (gcc-mirror/gcc)

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive search of the LLVM codebase and identified all the key C++ source files that implement stack protection mechanisms against buffer overflow attacks. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Summary of Stack Protection Mechanisms in LLVM

**Created `/workspace/answer.json` with findings:**

### 1. **StackProtector LLVM Pass** 
- **Files**: `llvm/lib/CodeGen/StackProtector.cpp` and `llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/StackProtector.h`
- **Primary Class**: `StackProtector` (FunctionPass)
- **Key Functions**: `InsertStackProtectors()`, `CreateFailBB()`, `SSPLayoutAnalysis::requiresStackProtector()`

### 2. **SafeStack Pass**
- **Files**: `llvm/lib/CodeGen/SafeStack.cpp` and `llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/SafeStack.h`
- **Primary Classes**: `SafeStack`, `SafeStackPass`, `SafeStackLegacyPass`
- **Purpose**: Separates stack into safe and unsafe regions to prevent certain classes of stack attacks

### 3. **SafeStack Layout Management**
- **Files**: `llvm/lib/CodeGen/SafeStackLayout.cpp` and `llvm/lib/CodeGen/SafeStackLayout.h`
- **Primary Class**: `SafeStackLayout`

### 4. **SafeStack Runtime Support**
- **File**: `compiler-rt/lib/safestack/safestack.cpp`
- **Purpose**: Runtime allocation/deallocation of unsafe stack memory

### 5. **Stack Guard Failure Handler** ⭐
- **Files**: `libc/src/compiler/generic/__stack_chk_fail.cpp` and `libc/src/compiler/__stack_chk_fail.h`
- **Primary Symbols**: `__stack_chk_fail()` (abort on corruption), `__stack_chk_guard` (guard variable)

### 6. **Additional Memory Safety Instrumentation** (in `llvm/lib/Transforms/Instrumentation/`)
- `AddressSanitizer.cpp` - Stack buffer overflow detection
- `HWAddressSanitizer.cpp` - Hardware-assisted stack tagging
- `MemorySanitizer.cpp` - Uninitialized memory detection
- `MemProfInstru

(llvm/lib/CodeGen/StackProtector.cpp, llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/StackProtector.h)**: The primary LLVM pass that inserts stack protector checks into functions. The StackProtector class is a FunctionPass that implements the stack smashing protection mechanism by loading a guard value before local variable allocations and checking it after (on function exit). Key functions include InsertStackProtectors() which inserts the prologue and epilogue code, CreateFailBB() which creates the failure path when the guard is corrupted, and SSPLayoutAnalysis which determines which functions require protection.\\n\\n2. **SafeStack Pass (llvm/lib/CodeGen/SafeStack.cpp, llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/SafeStack.h)**: Implements the SafeStack instrumentation pass that separates the stack into safe and unsafe portions. The SafeStack class (llvm/lib/CodeGen/SafeStack.cpp) performs the actual IR transformation, while SafeStackPass and SafeStackLegacyPass provide the pass interfaces. This mechanism protects against stack-based attacks by placing dangerous allocations (arrays, structures containing arrays) onto an explicitly managed unsafe stack.\\n\\n3. **SafeStackLayout (llvm/lib/CodeGen/SafeStackLayout.cpp, llvm/lib/CodeGen/SafeStackLayout.h)**: Manages the frame layout for the unsafe stack used by SafeStack, determining how allocations are arranged in memory.\\n\\n4. **SafeStack Runtime (compiler-rt/lib/safestack/safestack.cpp)**: Provides runtime support for SafeStack, including allocation and deallocation of unsafe stack memory for threads.\\n\\n5. **Stack Protector Runtime (__stack_chk_fail implementation): Located in libc/src/compiler/generic/__stack_chk_fail.cpp, this provides the actual __stack_chk_fail() function called when stack corruption is detected. It prints \\\"stack smashing detected\\\" and aborts execution. The __stack_chk_guard variable (also in this file) contains the guard value used to detect corruption. The header declaration is in libc/src/compiler/__stack_chk_fail.h.\\n\\n6. **Memory Safety Instrumentation (llvm/lib/Transforms/Instrumentation/)**: Additional stack-related memory safety instrumentation is provided through:\\n   - AddressSanitizer.cpp: Instruments stack memory to detect use-after-return and buffer overflows\\n   - HWAddressSanitizer.cpp: Uses hardware-assisted stack tagging for memory safety\\n   - MemorySanitizer.cpp: Detects use of uninitialized stack memory\\n   - MemProfInstrumentation.cpp: Profiles stack allocations for memory usage analysis\\n\\nThe call chain for stack protection is: StackProtector (detects guard corruption) \u2192 calls __stack_chk_fail() via RTLIB::STACKPROTECTOR_CHECK_FAIL \u2192 writes error message to stderr and calls abort(), while SafeStack operates at a different level by separating stack regions to prevent specific classes of attacks.\"\n}\n",
